as kernel.\n * Matches torch.nn.functional.conv3d with groups=C (depthwise).\n */\nstatic void cpu_depthwise_conv3d_ref(const std::vector<__hip_bfloat16>& in_bf16,\n                                     const std::vector<__hip_bfloat16>& w_bf16,\n                                     const std::vector<__hip_bfloat16>& bias_bf16, std::vector<float>& out_f32, int B,\n                                     int C, int D, int H, int W, int C_out, int D_out, int H_out, int W_out) {\n    out_f32.assign(static_cast<size_t>(B) * C_out * D_out * H_out * W_out, 0.f);\n    const int stride_d = 1, stride_h = 1, stride_w = 1;\n    const int dil_d = 1, dil_h = 1, dil_w = 1;\n\n    for (int b = 0; b < B; ++b) {\n        for (int oc = 0; oc < C_out; ++oc) {\n            const int ic = oc;\n            const float bias = bf16_to_float(bias_bf16[static_cast<size_t>(oc)]);\n            for (int od = 0; od < D_out; ++od) {\n                for (int oh = 0; oh < H_out; ++oh) {\n                    for (int ow = 0; ow < W_out; ++ow) {\n                        float acc = bias;\n                        for (int kd = 0; kd < KD; ++kd) {\n                            for (int kh = 0; kh < KH; ++kh) {\n                                for (int kw = 0; kw < KW; ++kw) {\n                                    const int id = od * stride_d - PaddingD + kd * dil_d;\n                                    const int ih = oh * stride_h - PaddingH + kh * dil_h;\n                                    const int iw = ow * stride_w - PaddingW + kw * dil_w;\n                                    if (id < 0 || id >= D || ih < 0 || ih >= H || iw < 0 || iw >= W) {\n                                        continue;\n                                    }\n                                    const float iv =\n                                        bf16_to_float(in_bf16[lin5(B, C, D, H, W, b, ic, id, ih, iw)]);\n                                    const float wv = bf16_to_float(w_bf16[lin_w(oc, kd, kh, kw)]);\n                                    acc += iv * wv;\n                                }\n                            }\n                        }\n                        out_f32[lin5(B, C_out, D_out, H_out, W_out, b, oc, od, oh, ow)] = acc;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nstatic void print_bytes_line(const char* label, size_t bytes) {\n    const double mib = static_cast<double>(bytes) / (1024.0 * 1024.0);\n    printf(\"  %-14s %10zu B  (%8.2f MiB)\\n\", label, bytes, mib);\n}\n\nstatic void print_run_header(int device_id) {\n    hipDeviceProp_t prop{};\n    HIP_CHECK(hipGetDeviceProperties(&prop, device_id));\n    printf(\"\\n\");\n    printf(\"=== Depthwise Conv3D BF16 (%s) ===\\n\", KERNEL_SGB ? \"sgb (sched_group_barrier variant)\" : void print_problem_and_memory(int B, int C, int D, int H, int W, int C_out, int D_out, int H_out, int W_out,\n                                     size_t n_in, size_t n_out, size_t n_w, size_t n_bias) {\n    const size_t bsz = sizeof(__hip_bfloat16);\n    const size_t bytes_in = n_in * bsz;\n    const size_t bytes_out = n_out * bsz;\n    const size_t bytes_w = n_w * bsz;\n    const size_t bytes_bias = n_bias * bsz;\n    const size_t bytes_dev = bytes_in + bytes_out + bytes_w + bytes_bias;\n\n    printf(\"\\n--- Problem (case3-style depthwise) ---\\n\");\n    printf(\"  Input NCHW:   [%d, %d, %d, %d, %d]  BF16\\n\", B, C, D, H, W);\n    printf(\"  Weight:       [%d, 1, %d, %d, %d]  BF16  (groups=%d depthwise)\\n\", C_out, KD, KH, KW, C);\n    printf(\"  Output NCHW:  [%d, %d, %d, %d, %d]  BF16\\n\", B, C_out, D_out, H_out, W_out);\n    printf(\"  stride=(1,1,1)  dilation=(1,1,1)  padding=(%d,%d,%d)\\n\", PaddingD, PaddingH, PaddingW);\n\n    printf(\"\\n--- Device buffers ---\\n\");\n    print_bytes_line(\"input\", bytes_in);\n    print_bytes_line(\"output\", bytes_out);\n    print_bytes_line(\"weights\", bytes_w);\n    print_bytes_line(\"bias\", bytes_bias);\n    print_bytes_line(\"total alloc\", bytes_dev);\n}\n\nstatic void print_kernel_config(dim3 grid, dim3 block) {\n    const long long total_blocks = static_cast<long long>(grid.x) * grid.y * grid.z;\n    const int threads_per_block = block.x * block.y * block.z;\n    const long long total_threads = total_blocks * threads_per_block;\n\n    printf(\"\\n--- Kernel configuration ---\\n\");\n    printf(\"  Kernel symbol: conv_depthwise3d_hip   (__launch_bounds__(256, 1) in HIP source)\\n\");\n    printf(\"  Compile-time: KD=%d KH=%d KW=%d  PaddingD/H/W=%d/%d/%d  BLOCK_H=%d BLOCK_W=%d total_threads);\n}\n\nstatic void print_performance(double avg_ms, int niter, int B, int C_out, int D_out, int H_out, int W_out, size_t n_in,\n                              size_t n_out, size_t n_w, size_t n_bias) {\n    const double sec = static_cast<double>(avg_ms) / 1000.0;\n    const double gflops =\n        (2.0 * static_cast<double>(B) * C_out * D_out * H_out * W_out * 1.0 * KD * KH * KW) / Let me look at the kernel descriptor in the ISA to see GRANULATED_WORKITEM_VGPR_COUNT.\n\nLet me check the binary descriptor encoding. The `.amdhsa_next_free_vgpr 155` is the raw count. The granulated count = (ceil(155/G) - 1) encoded in bits. Let me just compute possible G values:\n- G=4: ceil(155/4)=39, alloc=156. floor(512/156)=3.\n- G=8: ceil(155/8)=20, alloc=160. floor(512/160)=3.\n- G=16: ceil(155/16)=10, alloc=160. floor(512/160)=3.\n\nAll give 3 blocks. For 4 blocks need alloc ≤128:\n- G=4: ≤128 → real ≤128.\n- G=8: ≤128 → real ≤128 (128 is multiple of 8).\n- G=16: ≤128 → real ≤128.\n\nFor 5 blocks need alloc ≤102 (floor(512/102)=5, but 102 not multiple of 8/16):\n- floor(512/alloc)≥5 → alloc ≤102.4 → alloc ≤102.\n- G=8: alloc must be multiple of 8 ≤102 → 96. So real ≤96.\n- G=16: alloc multiple of 16 ≤102 → 96. real ≤96.\n- G=4: alloc multiple of 4 ≤102 → 100. real ≤100.\n\nSo for 5 blocks, need real VGPR ≤ 96 (if G=8 or 16) or ≤100 (if G=4).\n\nLet me aim for ≤96 to be safe. Weight packing + input interleave should get there.\n\nNow let me also reconsider: the `__launch_bounds__(256, 1)` — the second arg (minBlocksPerMultiprocessor=1) is just a hint to the compiler, doesn't hard-limit occupancy. The compiler uses it for register allocation decisions. With hint=1, the compiler feels free to use up to 255 VGPRs (allowing 1+ blocks). If I change hint to a higher number, the compiler might limit VGPRs more aggressively (even spilling). But the task says keep `__launch_bounds__(256, 1)` unchanged. So I must keep it. That's 3*5*3 = 45 dwords. Hmm, 45 not 38. Because [KD][KH][KWR] pads each (d,h) row to 3 dwords (6 BF16) but only 5 BF16 are used. So 45 dwords with 15 wasted BF16 slots. Let me use contiguous for max savings.\n\n  Actually, let me reconsider. The MAC loop accesses weights in order d,h,w. With contiguous packing, weight for (d,h,w) is at `weight_packed[ki/2]` half `ki&1` where ki = d*KH*KW + h*KW + w. Since the loop is fully unrolled, these are constants. The compiler can fold. Good.\n\n  But there's a subtlety: for the interleaved MAC, I process 2 weights at a time (w and w+1) which are exactly the 2 halves of one packed dword! So I can load `weight_packed[ki/2]` once and use both halves for the 2 MACs. That's elegant — the packed weight dword aligns with the 2-wide MAC processing.\n\n  Let me reconsider the MAC structure. For output ow (sum0), at kernel (d,h,w) and (d,h,w+1):\n  - fmac sum0, weight[kw=w], input[pos(ow,w)]\n  - fmac sum0, weight[kw=w+1], input[pos(ow,w+1)]\n  These two weights are the lo and hi halves of `weight_packed[base_ki/2]` where base_ki = d*KH*KW + h*KW + w (w even). \n\n  And the input for these two is exactly the loaded dword `dw` = [input[pos(ow,w)], input[pos(ow,w+1)]] = [lo, hi].\n\n  So: `fmac sum0, cvt(weight_dw.lo), cvt(dw.lo); fmac sum0, cvt(weight_dw.hi), cvt(dw.hi)`.\n\n  For sum1 (output ow+1), at kernel w and w+1:\n  - fmac sum1, weight[kw=w], input[pos(ow+1,w)] = weight[w] * dw.hi   (since pos(ow+1,w)=pos(ow,w+1)=dw.hi)\n  - fmac sum1, weight[kw=w+1], input[pos(ow+1,w+1)] = weight[w+1] * next_dw.lo  (pos(ow+1,w+1)=pos(ow,w+2)=next_dw.lo)\n\n  So sum1 uses the SAME weight dword (lo for kw=w, hi for kw=w+1) but different input halves.\n\nThis is clean. Let me structure the inner loop over (d, h, w_pack):\n\n```\nfloat sum0 = bias, sum1 = bias;\nuint32_t next_dw = 0;\n// preload first input dword for (d=0,h=0,w_pack=0)\nuint32_t in_dw = ds_read_b32(s_input + srci0, off(d=0,h=0,w=0));\nfor d in 0..KD:\n  for h in 0..KH:\n    for w_pack in 0..KWR:   // 0,1,2 → w=0,2,4\n      // at this point in_dw = dword for (d,h,w_pack)\n      // load NEXT dword (for next iteration), except on last iteration\n      if not last(d,h,w_pack):\n        next_dw = ds_read_b32(s_input + srci0, off(d,h,next w_pack));\n      // get weight dword\n      uint32_t wt_dw = weight_packed[ki(d,h,w_pack)/2];   // compile-time index\n      // extract halves\n      bf16 wt_lo = lo(wt_dw), wt_hi = hi(wt_dw);\n      bf16 in_lo = lo(in_dw), in_hi = hi(in_dw);\n      // sum0: weight[w]*in_lo, weight[w+1]*in_hi (if w+1<KW)\n      fmac sum0, (float)wt_lo, (float)in_lo;\n      if (w+1 < KW) fmac sum0, (float)wt_hi, (float)in_hi;\n      // sum1: weight[w]*in_hi, weight[w+1]*next_in_lo (if w+1<KW)\n      fmac sum1, (float)wt_lo, (float)in_hi;\n      if (w+1 < KW) fmac sum1, (float)wt_hi, (float)lo(next_dw);\n      // advance\n      in_dw = next_dw;\n```\n\nWait, there's an issue with the loop boundary and preloading. If I change to load-3-MAC-10 per (d,h) with the dw[3] scoped inside the (d,h) loop, the compiler's register allocator, after unrolling, sees 15 separate dw[3] arrays. Whether it reuses VGPRs depends on liveness analysis: if dw[3] of site (d,h) is dead before dw[3] of site (d,h+1) is defined, the allocator reuses. The fmacs of site (d,h) consume dw[3], making it dead. Then site (d,h+1)'s reads define new dw[3]. So liveness: site (d,h)'s dw[3] dies before site (d,h+1)'s dw[3] is born → SAME VGPRs reused. \n\nBUT — the compiler's instruction scheduler (not just allocator) might move site (d,h+1)'s reads early (before site (d,h)'s fmacs) to hide LDS latency. If it does, site (d,h+1)'s dw[3] is born while site (d,h)'s dw[3] is still alive → 6 live. The allocator then needs 6 VGPRs for dw. \n\nWith minBlocks=1, the scheduler favors latency hiding → likely hoists → 6+ live. But 6 is still way less than 45. And the scheduler won't hoist ALL 15 sites' reads (that's 45, with no benefit since they'd all wait on the same lgkmcnt). It'll hoist maybe 1-2 sites ahead. So ~6-12 dw live.
